style="padding-left:1.0em">Fahrenheit</th>\n<td>&#8722;135</td>\n<td></td>\n<td>&#8722;45</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n</div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>67P/Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko</b> (abbreviated as <b>67P</b> or <b>67P/C-G</b>) is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jupiter-family_comet" title="Jupiter-family comet">Jupiter-family comet</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yfernandez_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-yfernandez-8">[8]</a></sup> originally from the <a href="/wiki/Kuiper_belt" title="Kuiper belt">Kuiper belt</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20141210-SB_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20141210-SB-9">[9]</a></sup> with a current <a href="/wiki/Orbital_period" title="Orbital period">orbital period</a> of 6.45 years,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpldata_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-jpldata-1">[1]</a></sup> a rotation period of approximately 12.4 hours<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mottola2014_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mottola2014-7">[7]</a></sup> and a maximum velocity of 135,000&#160;km/h (38&#160;km/s; 84,000&#160;mph).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA-faq_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESA-faq-10">[10]</a></sup> Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko is approximately 4.3 by 4.1&#160;km (2.7 by 2.5&#160;mi) at its longest and widest dimensions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67P_size_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-67P_size-11">[11]</a></sup> It was first observed on <a href="/wiki/Photographic_plate" title="Photographic plate">photographic plates</a> in 1969 by Soviet astronomers <a href="/wiki/Klim_Churyumov" title="Klim Churyumov">Klim Ivanovych Churyumov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Gerasimenko" title="Svetlana Gerasimenko">Svetlana Ivanovna Gerasimenko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naming_of_comets" title="Naming of comets">after whom it is named</a>. It came to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perihelion_and_aphelion" title="Perihelion and aphelion">perihelion</a> (closest approach to the Sun) on 13 August 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20150813_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20150813-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yoshida_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yoshida-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MPC_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-MPC-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kinoshita_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kinoshita-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko was the destination of the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Rosetta_(spacecraft)" title="Rosetta (spacecraft)"><i>Rosetta</i></a> mission, launched on 2 March 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krolikowska2003_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Krolikowska2003-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-201401017_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-201401017-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20140805_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20140805-17">[17]</a></sup> <i>Rosetta</i> <a href="/wiki/Space_rendezvous" title="Space rendezvous">rendezvoused</a> with Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko on 6 August 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fischer2014-08-06_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fischer2014-08-06-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bauer2014_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bauer2014-19">[19]</a></sup> and entered orbit on 10 September 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20140910_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-esa20140910-20">[20]</a></sup> <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> lander, <a href="/wiki/Philae_(spacecraft)" title="Philae (spacecraft)"><i>Philae</i></a>, landed on the comet\'s surface on 12 November 2014, becoming the first spacecraft to land on a <a href="/wiki/Comet_nucleus" title="Comet nucleus">comet nucleus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20141112-DCA_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20141112-DCA-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20141112-KC_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20141112-KC-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcland_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcland-23">[23]</a></sup> On 30 September 2016, the <i>Rosetta</i> spacecraft ended its mission by landing on the comet in its Ma\'at region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newsci20160930_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-newsci20160930-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space20160930_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-space20160930-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Discovery"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Discovery</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Shape"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Shape</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Surface"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Surface</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Gates"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Gates</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Surface_changes"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Surface changes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Orbit_and_rotation"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Orbit and rotation</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#2015_perihelion"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">2015 perihelion</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Rosetta_mission"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext"><i>Rosetta</i> mission</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Advance_work"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Advance work</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Rendezvous_and_orbit"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Rendezvous and orbit</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Landing"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Landing</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Science"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Science</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Future_missions"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Future missions</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Gallery"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Gallery</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery">Discovery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Discovery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko was discovered in 1969 by <a href="/wiki/Klim_Churyumov" title="Klim Churyumov">Klim Ivanovich Churyumov</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Taras_Shevchenko_National_University_of_Kyiv#Astronomical_Observatory" title="Taras Shevchenko National University of Kyiv">Kiev University\'s Astronomical Observatory</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iau61_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-iau61-26">[26]</a></sup> who examined a photograph that had been exposed for comet <a href="/wiki/32P/Comas_Sol%C3%A0" title="32P/Comas Sol&#224;">Comas Sol&#224;</a> by <a href="/wiki/Svetlana_Gerasimenko" title="Svetlana Gerasimenko">Svetlana Ivanovna Gerasimenko</a> on 11 September 1969 at the <a href="/wiki/Fesenkov_Astrophysical_Institute" title="Fesenkov Astrophysical Institute">Alma-Ata Astrophysical Institute</a>, near Alma-Ata (now <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>), the then-capital city of <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic">Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. Churyumov found a cometary object near the edge of the plate, but assumed that this was comet Comas Sol&#224;.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kronk_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kronk-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After returning to his home institute in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>, Churyumov examined all the photographic plates more closely. On 22 October, about a month after the photograph was taken, he discovered that the object could not be Comas Sol&#224;, because it was about 1.8 degrees off the expected position. Further scrutiny produced a faint image of Comas Sol&#224; at its expected position on the plate, thus proving the other object to be a different body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kronk_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kronk-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shape">Shape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Shape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><span class="mw-3d-wrapper" data-label="3D"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Comet_67P-Churyumov-Gerasimenko.stl"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2880" data-file-width="5120" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Comet_67P-Churyumov-Gerasimenko.stl/220px-Comet_67P-Churyumov-Gerasimenko.stl.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Comet_67P-Churyumov-Gerasimenko.stl/330px-Comet_67P-Churyumov-Gerasimenko.stl.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Comet_67P-Churyumov-Gerasimenko.stl/440px-Comet_67P-Churyumov-Gerasimenko.stl.png 2x" width="220"/></a></span> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Comet_67P-Churyumov-Gerasimenko.stl" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3D_modelling" title="3D modelling">3D model</a> of 67P by ESA (click to rotate)</div></div></div>\n<p>The comet consists of two lobes connected by a narrower neck, with the larger lobe measuring about 4.1&#215;3.3&#215;1.8&#160;km (2.5&#215;2.1&#215;1.1&#160;mi) and the smaller one about 2.6&#215;2.3&#215;1.8&#160;km (1.6&#215;1.4&#215;1.1&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20150122_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-esa20150122-3">[3]</a></sup> With each orbit the comet loses matter, as gas and dust are evaporated away by the sun. It is estimated that currently a layer with an average thickness of about 1&#160;&#177;&#160;0.5&#160;m (3.3&#160;&#177;&#160;1.6&#160;ft) is lost per orbit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The comet has a mass of approximately 10 billion tonnes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mass_density_2016_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-mass_density_2016-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The two-lobe shape of the comet is the result of a gentle, low-velocity collision of two objects. The "terraces", layers of the interior of the comet that have been exposed by partial stripping of outer layers during its existence, are oriented in different directions in the two lobes, indicating that two objects fused to form Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo20150928_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo20150928-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Massironi2015_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Massironi2015-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Surface">Surface</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Surface">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:67P_Churyumov-Gerasimenko_surface.gif"><img alt="A black and white short animation of dust on the surface" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="490" data-file-width="490" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/67P_Churyumov-Gerasimenko_surface.gif/220px-67P_Churyumov-Gerasimenko_surface.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/67P_Churyumov-Gerasimenko_surface.gif/330px-67P_Churyumov-Gerasimenko_surface.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/67P_Churyumov-Gerasimenko_surface.gif/440px-67P_Churyumov-Gerasimenko_surface.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:67P_Churyumov-Gerasimenko_surface.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dust and <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray" title="Cosmic ray">cosmic rays</a> on the surface of the comet in 2016, with stars moving in the background</div></div></div>\n<p>There are 26 distinct regions on Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko, with each named after an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_deity" title="Egyptian deity">Egyptian deity</a>; regions on the large lobe are named after gods, whereas those on the small lobe are named after goddesses. 19 regions were defined in the northern hemisphere prior to <a href="/wiki/Equinox" title="Equinox">equinox</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ElMaarry2015_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-ElMaarry2015-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-space20150719_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-space20150719-32">[32]</a></sup> Later, when the southern hemisphere became illuminated, seven more regions were identified using the same naming convention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ElMaarry2016_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-ElMaarry2016-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20160224_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-esa20160224-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Region</th>\n<th>Terrain</th>\n<th>Region</th>\n<th>Terrain</th>\n<th>Region</th>\n<th>Terrain\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Maat" title="Maat">Ma\'at</a></td>\n<td>Dust covered\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ash_(deity)" title="Ash (deity)">Ash</a></td>\n<td>Dust covered\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Babi_(mythology)" title="Babi (mythology)">Babi</a></td>\n<td>Dust covered\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Set_(deity)" title="Set (deity)">Seth</a></td>\n<td>Pitted and brittle material\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Hatmehit" href="/wiki/Imhotep" title="Imhotep">Imhotep</a></td>\n<td>Smooth\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Anubis" title="Anubis">Anubis</a></td>\n<td>Smooth\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Mafdet" (deity)">Aker</a></td>\n<td>Rock-like\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Atum" title="Atum">Atum</a></td>\n<td>Rock-like\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Apis_(deity)" title="Apis (deity)">Apis</a></td>\n<td>Rock-like\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Khonsu" title="Khonsu">Khonsu</a></td>\n<td>Rock-like\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Bes" title="Bes">Bes</a></td>\n<td>Rock-like\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Anhur" title="Anhur">Anhur</a></td>\n<td>Rock-like, rather friable\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Geb" title="Geb">Geb</a></td>\n<td>Rock-like\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Sobek" title="Sobek">Sobek</a></td>\n<td>Rock-like\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Neith" title="Neith">Neith</a></td>\n<td>Rock-like\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Wosret" title="Wosret">Wosret</a></td>\n<td>Rock-like\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gates">Gates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Gates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Features described as <i>gates</i>, twin <a href="/wiki/Topographic_prominence" title="Topographic prominence">prominences</a> on the surface so named for their appearance,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="could use an image, anything actually looking like a gate would be exceedingly weird (October 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> have received names by the Rosetta Science Working Team. They are named after deceased members of the <i>Rosetta</i> team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Name</th>\n<th>Named after\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>C. Alexander Gate</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Claudia_Alexander" title="Claudia Alexander">Claudia Alexander</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>A. Coradini Gate</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Angioletta_Coradini" title="Angioletta Coradini">Angioletta Coradini</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Surface_changes">Surface changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Surface changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> lifetime, many changes were observed on the comet\'s surface, particularly when the comet was close to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perihelion" title="Perihelion">perihelion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ElMaarry2017_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-ElMaarry2017-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20170321_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-esa20170321-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa20170321_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa20170321-38">[38]</a></sup> These changes included evolving patterns of circular shapes in smooth terrains that at some point grew in size by a few meters per day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Groussin2015_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Groussin2015-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20150918_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-esa20150918-40">[40]</a></sup> A fracture in the neck region was also observed to grow in size; boulders tens of meters wide were displaced, sometimes travelling more than 100 meters; and patches of the ground were removed to expose new features. A number of collapsing cliffs have also been observed. One notable example in December 2015 was captured by <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> NAVCAM as a bright patch of light shining from the comet. <i>Rosetta</i> scientists determined that a large cliff had collapsed, making it the first landslide on a comet known to be associated with an outburst of activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pajola2017_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pajola2017-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wapo20170321_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-wapo20170321-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orbit_and_rotation">Orbit and rotation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Orbit and rotation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Comet_67P_orbit_perihelion_2015.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1127" data-file-width="1141" decoding="async" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Comet_67P_orbit_perihelion_2015.png/220px-Comet_67P_orbit_perihelion_2015.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Comet_67P_orbit_perihelion_2015.png/330px-Comet_67P_orbit_perihelion_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Comet_67P_orbit_perihelion_2015.png/440px-Comet_67P_orbit_perihelion_2015.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Comet_67P_orbit_perihelion_2015.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The orbit of 67P/Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko moves from just inside the orbit of Mars to just outside the orbit of Jupiter, seen here at perihelion in August 2015.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NavCam_Comet_67P_animation_20140806_(cropped).gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="360" decoding="async" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/NavCam_Comet_67P_animation_20140806_%28cropped%29.gif/170px-NavCam_Comet_67P_animation_20140806_%28cropped%29.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/NavCam_Comet_67P_animation_20140806_%28cropped%29.gif/255px-NavCam_Comet_67P_animation_20140806_%28cropped%29.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/NavCam_Comet_67P_animation_20140806_%28cropped%29.gif/340px-NavCam_Comet_67P_animation_20140806_%28cropped%29.gif 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NavCam_Comet_67P_animation_20140806_(cropped).gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This animation consists of 86 images acquired by <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> NavCam as it approached 67P in August 2014.</div></div></div>\n<p>Like the other comets of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jupiter-family_comet" title="Jupiter-family comet">Jupiter family</a>, Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko probably originated in the <a href="/wiki/Kuiper_belt" title="Kuiper belt">Kuiper belt</a> and was ejected towards the interior of the Solar System, where later encounters with <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a> successively changed its orbit.\n</p><p>Up to 1840, the comet\'s perihelion distance was 4&#160;<a href="/wiki/Astronomical_unit" title="Astronomical unit">AU</a> (600&#160;million&#160;<a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">km</a>), too far for the Sun to vaporize the nucleus. In 1840 Jupiter changed the orbit to a perihelion distance of 3&#160;AU (450&#160;million&#160;km), and later encounters further decreased that distance to 2.77&#160;AU (414&#160;million&#160;km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RosTarget_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-RosTarget-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 1959, a close encounter with Jupiter<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpl-close_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-jpl-close-44">[44]</a></sup> moved Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko\'s perihelion inward to about 1.29&#160;AU (193&#160;million&#160;km), where it remains today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kinoshita_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kinoshita-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RosTarget_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-RosTarget-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko\'s perihelion passage in 2009, its rotational period was 12.76 hours. During this perihelion passage, it decreased to 12.4 hours, which likely happened because of <a href="/wiki/Sublimation_(phase_transition)" title="Sublimation (phase transition)">sublimation</a>-induced <a href="/wiki/Torque" title="Torque">torque</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mottola2014_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mottola2014-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_perihelion">2015 perihelion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2015 perihelion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As of  September&#160;2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko\'s <a href="/wiki/Comet_nucleus" title="Comet nucleus">nucleus</a> had an <a href="/wiki/Apparent_magnitude" title="Apparent magnitude">apparent magnitude</a> of roughly 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MPC_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-MPC-13">[13]</a></sup> It came to perihelion on 13 August 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20150813_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20150813-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yoshida_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yoshida-12">[12]</a></sup> From December 2014 until September 2015, it had an <a href="/wiki/Elongation_(astronomy)" title="Elongation (astronomy)">elongation</a> less than 45 degrees from the Sun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MPC-emp_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-MPC-emp-45">[45]</a></sup> On 10 February 2015, it went through <a href="/wiki/Solar_conjunction" title="Solar conjunction">solar conjunction</a> when it was 5 degrees from the Sun and was 3.3&#160;AU (490&#160;million&#160;km) from Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MPC-emp_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-MPC-emp-45">[45]</a></sup> It crossed the <a href="/wiki/Celestial_equator" title="Celestial equator">celestial equator</a> on 5 May 2015 and became easiest to see from the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MPC-emp_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-MPC-emp-45">[45]</a></sup> Even right after perihelion when it was in the constellation of <a href="/wiki/Gemini_(constellation)" title="Gemini (constellation)">Gemini</a>, it only brightened to about apparent magnitude 12, and required a telescope to be seen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yoshida_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Yoshida-12">[12]</a></sup> As of  July&#160;2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the comet had a total magnitude of about 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MPC_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-MPC-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rosetta_mission"><i>Rosetta</i> mission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rosetta mission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Rosetta_(spacecraft)" title="Rosetta (spacecraft)">Rosetta (spacecraft)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philae_(spacecraft)" title="Philae (spacecraft)">Philae (spacecraft)</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Rosetta_spacecraft" title="Timeline of Rosetta spacecraft">Timeline of Rosetta spacecraft</a></div>\n<p>Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko was the destination of the <i><a href="/wiki/Rosetta_(spacecraft)" title="Rosetta (spacecraft)">Rosetta</a></i> mission, launched in 2004, which rendezvoused with it in 2014 and was the first mission to land a <a href="/wiki/Space_probe" title="Space probe">space probe</a> on a comet.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advance_work">Advance work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Advance work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rosetta%27s_first_sighting_of_its_target_in_2014_%E2%80%93_narrow_angle_view_(14813677376).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="559" data-file-width="766" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Rosetta%27s_first_sighting_of_its_target_in_2014_%E2%80%93_narrow_angle_view_%2814813677376%29.jpg/220px-Rosetta%27s_first_sighting_of_its_target_in_2014_%E2%80%93_narrow_angle_view_%2814813677376%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Rosetta%27s_first_sighting_of_its_target_in_2014_%E2%80%93_narrow_angle_view_%2814813677376%29.jpg/330px-Rosetta%27s_first_sighting_of_its_target_in_2014_%E2%80%93_narrow_angle_view_%2814813677376%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Rosetta%27s_first_sighting_of_its_target_in_2014_%E2%80%93_narrow_angle_view_%2814813677376%29.jpg/440px-Rosetta%27s_first_sighting_of_its_target_in_2014_%E2%80%93_narrow_angle_view_%2814813677376%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rosetta%27s_first_sighting_of_its_target_in_2014_%E2%80%93_narrow_angle_view_(14813677376).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>First image of the comet taken by <i>Rosetta</i> with <a href="/wiki/Messier_107" title="Messier 107">Messier 107</a> in view, 21 March 2014</div></div></div>\n<p>As preparation for the <i>Rosetta</i> mission, <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a> pictures taken on 12 March 2003 were closely analysed. An overall 3D model was constructed and computer-generated images were created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STScI-2003-26_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-STScI-2003-26-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 25 April 2012, the most detailed observations until that time were taken with the 2-metre Faulkes Telescope by N. Howes, G. Sostero and E. Guido while it was at its aphelion.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>On 6 June 2014, water vapor was detected being released at a rate of roughly 1&#160;L/s (0.26&#160;USgal/s) when <i>Rosetta</i> was 360,000&#160;km (220,000&#160;mi) from Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko and 3.9&#160;AU (580&#160;million&#160;km) from the Sun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blog140623_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-blog140623-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20140630_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20140630-48">[48]</a></sup> On 14 July 2014, images taken by <i>Rosetta</i> showed that its <a href="/wiki/Comet_nucleus" title="Comet nucleus">nucleus</a> is irregular in shape with two distinct lobes. Two explanations were proposed at the time: that its shape may have resulted from <a href="/wiki/Asymmetry" title="Asymmetry">asymmetric</a> erosion due to ice sublimating from its surface to leave behind its lobed shape. Newer evidence supports the <a href="/wiki/Contact_binary_(small_Solar_System_body)" title="Contact binary (small Solar System body)">contact binary</a> model. The size of the nucleus was estimated to be 3.5&#215;4&#160;km (2.2&#215;2.5&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20140805_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20140805-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astronomy20140717_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-astronomy20140717-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skytel20140717_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-skytel20140717-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rendezvous_and_orbit">Rendezvous and orbit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rendezvous and orbit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:542px;max-width:542px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:269px;max-width:269px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:200px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory.gif"><img alt="" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="560" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory.gif/267px-Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory.gif/401px-Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory.gif/534px-Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory.gif 2x" width="267"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Animation of <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> trajectory from <span class="nowrap">2 March</span> 2004 to <span class="nowrap">9 September</span> 2016 <br/> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:magenta; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<i>Rosetta</i></span>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:lime; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;67P</span>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:blue; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Earth</span>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:maroon; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Mars</span>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:Cyan; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;21 Lutetia</span>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:Gold; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;2867 &#352;teins</span></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:269px;max-width:269px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:200px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory_around_67P.gif"><img alt="" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="560" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory_around_67P.gif/267px-Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory_around_67P.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory_around_67P.gif/401px-Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory_around_67P.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory_around_67P.gif/534px-Animation_of_Rosetta_trajectory_around_67P.gif 2x" width="267"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Animation of <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> orbit around 67P from <span class="nowrap">1 August</span> 2014 to <span class="nowrap">31 March</span> 2015<br/> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:magenta; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<i>Rosetta</i></span>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:Lime; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;67P</span></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Beginning in May 2014, <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> velocity was reduced by 780&#160;m/s (2,800&#160;km/h; 1,700&#160;mph) with a <a href="/wiki/Delta-v" title="Delta-v">series of thruster firings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20140805_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20140805-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csm20140804_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-csm20140804-51">[51]</a></sup> Ground controllers rendezvoused <i>Rosetta</i> with Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko on 6 August 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fischer2014-08-06_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fischer2014-08-06-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bauer2014_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bauer2014-19">[19]</a></sup> This was done by reducing <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> relative <a href="/wiki/Velocity" title="Velocity">velocity</a> to 1&#160;m/s (4&#160;km/h; 2&#160;mph). <i>Rosetta</i> entered orbit on 10 September, at about 30&#160;km (19&#160;mi) from the nucleus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fischer2014-08-06_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fischer2014-08-06-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bauer2014_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bauer2014-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lakdawalla2014-08-15_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lakdawalla2014-08-15-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landing">Landing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Landing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information on the comet landing: <a href="/wiki/Philae_(spacecraft)#Mission" title="Philae (spacecraft)">Philae (spacecraft) &#167;&#160;Mission</a></div>\n<p>Descent of a small <a href="/wiki/Lander_(spacecraft)" title="Lander (spacecraft)">lander</a> occurred on 12 November 2014. <i><a href="/wiki/Philae_(spacecraft)" title="Philae (spacecraft)">Philae</a></i> is a 100&#160;kg (220&#160;lb) <a href="/wiki/Space_probe" title="Space probe">robotic probe</a> that set down on the surface with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacecraft_lander_landing_gear" title="Spacecraft lander landing gear">landing gear</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20140805_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20140805-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20141110-KC_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20141110-KC-53">[53]</a></sup> The landing site has been christened <i>Agilkia</i> in honour of <a href="/wiki/Agilkia_Island" title="Agilkia Island">Agilkia Island</a>, where the temples of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philae_Island" title="Philae Island">Philae Island</a> were relocated after the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Aswan_Low_Dam" title="Aswan Low Dam">Aswan Dam</a> flooded the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcnews20141104_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcnews20141104-54">[54]</a></sup> The acceleration due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gravitation" title="Gravitation">gravity</a> on the surface of Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko has been estimated for simulation purposes at 10<sup>&#8722;3</sup>&#160;m/s<sup>2</sup>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hilchenbach2004_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hilchenbach2004-55">[55]</a></sup> or about one ten-thousandth of that on Earth.\n</p><p>Because of its low relative mass, landing on the comet involved certain technical considerations to keep <i>Philae</i> anchored. The probe contains an array of mechanisms designed to manage Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko\'s low gravity, including a <a href="/wiki/Cold_gas_thruster" title="Cold gas thruster">cold gas thruster</a>, harpoons, landing-leg-mounted ice screws, and a flywheel to keep it oriented during its descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn20141113_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn20141113-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-register20141112_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-register20141112-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-discovery20141112_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-discovery20141112-58">[58]</a></sup> During the event, the thruster and the harpoons failed to operate, and the ice screws did not gain a grip. The lander bounced twice and only came to rest when it made contact with the surface for the third time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20141113-DCA_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20141113-DCA-59">[59]</a></sup> two hours after first contact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skytel20141112_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-skytel20141112-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Contact with <i>Philae</i> was lost on 15 November 2014 because of dropping battery power. The European Space Operations Centre briefly reestablished communications on 14 June 2015 and reported a healthy spacecraft but communications were lost again soon after.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nature20150614_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-nature20150614-61">[61]</a></sup> On 2 September 2016, <i>Philae</i> was located in photographs taken by the <i>Rosetta</i> orbiter. It had come to rest in a crack with only its body and two legs visible. While the discovery solves the question of the lander\'s disposition, it also allows project scientists to properly contextualise the data it returned from the comet\'s surface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science">Science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4267" data-file-width="7267" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg/220px-Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg/330px-Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg/440px-Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crescent_Comet_67P.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>False colour image of the comet outgassing, 15 April 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>The composition of <a href="/wiki/Water_vapor" title="Water vapor">water vapor</a> from Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko, as determined by the <i>Rosetta</i> spacecraft, is substantially different from that found on Earth. The ratio of <a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium">deuterium</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> in the water from the comet was determined to be three times that found for terrestrial water. This makes it unlikely that water found on Earth came from comets such as Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20141210-SB_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20141210-SB-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20141210-DCA_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20141210-DCA-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20141210-KC_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20141210-KC-64">[64]</a></sup> On 22 January 2015, NASA reported that, between June and August 2014, the comet released increasing amounts of water vapor, up to tenfold as much.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20150122_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20150122-65">[65]</a></sup> On 23 January 2015, the journal <i><a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science</a></i> published a special issue of scientific studies related to the comet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20150123_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-SCI-20150123-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Measurements carried out before <i>Philae</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> batteries failed indicate that the dust layer could be as much as 20&#160;cm (8&#160;in) thick. Beneath that is hard ice, or a mixture of ice and dust. <a href="/wiki/Porosity" title="Porosity">Porosity</a> appears to increase toward the center of the comet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20141218_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-esa20141218-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The nucleus of Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko was found to have no magnetic field of its own after measurements were taken during <i>Philae</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> descent and landing by its ROMAP instrument and <i>Rosetta</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> RPC-MAG instrument. This suggests that magnetism may not have played a role in the early formation of the Solar System, as had previously been hypothesized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20150414_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-esa20150414-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nature20150414_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-nature20150414-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Rosetta_(spacecraft)#Instruments" title="Rosetta (spacecraft)">ALICE spectrograph</a> on <i>Rosetta</i> determined that <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">electrons</a> (within 1&#160;km or 0.6&#160;mi above the <a href="/wiki/Comet_nucleus" title="Comet nucleus">comet nucleus</a>) produced from <a href="/wiki/Photoionization" title="Photoionization">photoionization</a> of water <a href="/wiki/Molecule" title="Molecule">molecules</a> by <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">solar radiation</a>, and not <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">photons</a> from the Sun as thought earlier, are responsible for the degradation of water and <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> molecules released from the comet nucleus into its <a href="/wiki/Coma_(cometary)" title="Coma (cometary)">coma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20150602_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-20150602-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AA-20150602_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-AA-20150602-71">[71]</a></sup> Also, active pits, related to <a href="/wiki/Sinkhole" title="Sinkhole">sinkhole</a> collapses and possibly associated with outbursts are present on the comet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAT-20150702_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-NAT-20150702-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20150701_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20150701-73">[73]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Measurements by the COSAC and Ptolemy instruments on the <i>Philae</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> lander revealed sixteen <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">organic compounds</a>, four of which were seen for the first time on a comet, including <a href="/wiki/Acetamide" title="Acetamide">acetamide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acetone" title="Acetone">acetone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methyl_isocyanate" title="Methyl isocyanate">methyl isocyanate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Propionaldehyde" title="Propionaldehyde">propionaldehyde</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wapo20150730_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-wapo20150730-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa20150730_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-esa20150730-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20150731_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-SCI-20150731-76">[76]</a></sup>  Astrobiologists <a href="/wiki/Chandra_Wickramasinghe" title="Chandra Wickramasinghe">Chandra Wickramasinghe</a> and Max Wallis stated that some of the physical features detected on the comet\'s surface by <i>Rosetta</i> and <i>Philae</i>, such as its <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">organic</a>-rich crust, could be explained by the presence of <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">extraterrestrial</a> <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganisms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TG-20150705_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-TG-20150705-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SN-20150706_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-SN-20150706-78">[78]</a></sup> <i>Rosetta</i> program scientists dismissed the claim as "pure speculation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TT-20150706_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-TT-20150706-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_interstellar_and_circumstellar_molecules" title="List of interstellar and circumstellar molecules">Carbon-rich compounds</a> are common in the Solar System. Neither <i>Rosetta</i> nor <i>Philae</i> is equipped to search for direct evidence of <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TG-20150705_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-TG-20150705-77">[77]</a></sup> The only amino acid detected thus far on the comet is <a href="/wiki/Glycine" title="Glycine">glycine</a>, along with precursor molecules <a href="/wiki/Methylamine" title="Methylamine">methylamine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethylamine" title="Ethylamine">ethylamine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altwegg_2016_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Altwegg_2016-80">[80]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Solid organic compounds were also found in the dust particles emitted by the comet; the carbon in this organic material is bound in "very large macromolecular compounds", analogous to the insoluble organic matter in <a href="/wiki/Carbonaceous_chondrite" title="Carbonaceous chondrite">carbonaceous chondrite</a> meteorites. Scientists think that the observed cometary carbonaceous solid matter could have the same origin as the meteoritic insoluble organic matter, but suffered less modification before or after being incorporated into the comet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fray_2016_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fray_2016-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p><p>One of the most outstanding discoveries of the mission so far is the detection of large amounts of free molecular <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> (O<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br/>2</span>) gas surrounding the comet. Current solar system models suggest the molecular oxygen should have disappeared by the time 67P was created, about 4.6&#160;billion years ago in a violent and hot process that would have caused the oxygen to react with hydrogen and form water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bieler_2015_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bieler_2015-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Howel_2015_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Howel_2015-83">[83]</a></sup> Molecular oxygen has never before been detected in cometary comas. <i>In situ</i> measurements indicate that the O<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br/>2</span>/H<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br/>2</span>O ratio is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isotropic" title="Isotropic">isotropic</a> in the coma and does not change systematically with heliocentric distance, suggesting that primordial O<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br/>2</span> was incorporated into the nucleus during the comet\'s formation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bieler_2015_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bieler_2015-82">[82]</a></sup> Detection of molecular nitrogen (N<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br/>2</span>) in the comet suggests that its cometary grains formed in low-temperature conditions below 30&#160;K (&#8722;243&#160;&#176;C; &#8722;406&#160;&#176;F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rubin2015_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rubin2015-84">[84]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 July 2018, researchers reported that molecular oxygen is not made on the surface of comet 67P, a finding that supports the notion that the oxygen comes from the body of the comet, and may be primordial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heritier2018_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heritier2018-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imperial20180703_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-imperial20180703-86">[86]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_missions">Future missions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Future missions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/CAESAR_(spacecraft)" title="CAESAR (spacecraft)">CAESAR</a> is a proposed <a href="/wiki/Sample-return_mission" title="Sample-return mission">sample-return mission</a> aimed at returning to 67P/Churyumov&#8211;Gerasimenko, capturing <a href="/wiki/Regolith" title="Regolith">regolith</a> from the surface, and returning it to Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa20171220_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa20171220-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes20171219_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes20171219-88">[88]</a></sup> This mission is competing in NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/New_Frontiers_program" title="New Frontiers program">New Frontiers</a> mission 4 selection process, and as of December 2017 is one of two finalists in the program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes20171220_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes20171220-89">[89]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">Gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul 10 December 2014\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="5600" data-file-width="4500" decoding="async" height="28"
